2:19:971:0:14:72:261:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:Coalition Formation in Political Games
2:20:1009:14:14:72:345:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:Daron Acemoglu, Georgy Egorov, and Konstantin Sonin
2:21:1060:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 12749
2:22:1088:14:14:72:148:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:December 2006
2:23:1101:14:28:72:182:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. C71,D71,D74
2:24:1120:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:F:ABSTRACT
2:25:1128:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:We study the formation of a ruling coalition in political environments.  Each individual is endowed
2:26:1227:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:with a level of political power.  The ruling coalition consists of a subset of the individuals in the society
2:27:1336:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:and decides the distribution of resources.  A ruling coalition needs to contain enough powerful members
2:28:1439:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:to win against any alternative coalition that may challenge it, and it needs to be self-enforcing, in the
2:29:1544:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:sense that none of its sub-coalitions should be able to secede and become the new ruling coalition.
2:30:1643:14:14:72:539:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:We first present an axiomatic approach that captures these notions and determines a (generically)
2:31:1740:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:unique ruling coalition.  We then construct a simple dynamic game that encompasses these ideas and
2:32:1838:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:prove that the sequentially weakly dominant equilibria (and the Markovian trembling hand perfect
2:33:1934:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:equilibria) of this game coincide with the set of ruling coalitions of the axiomatic approach.  We also
2:34:2037:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:show the equivalence of these notions to the core of a related non-transferable utility cooperative game.
2:35:2142:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:In all cases, the nature of the ruling coalition is determined by the power constraint, which requires
2:36:2244:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:F:that the ruling coalition be powerful enough, and by the enforcement constraint, which imposes that
2:37:2343:14:14:72:540:420:12:Times:12:Times:F:no sub-coalition of the ruling coalition that commands a majority is self-enforcing.  The key insight
2:38:2444:14:14:72:540:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:that emerges from this characterization is that the coalition is made self-enforcing precisely by the
2:39:2545:14:14:72:540:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:failure of its winning sub-coalitions to be self-enforcing.  This is most simply illustrated by the following
2:40:2654:14:14:72:540:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:simple finding: with a simple majority rule, while three-person (or larger) coalitions can be self-enforcing,
2:41:2763:14:14:72:540:364:12:Times:12:Times:F:two-person coalitions are generically not self-enforcing.  Therefore, the reasoning in this paper suggests
2:42:2869:14:14:72:540:350:12:Times:12:Times:F:that three-person juntas or councils should be more common than two-person ones.  In addition, we
2:43:2966:14:14:72:540:336:12:Times:12:Times:F:provide conditions under which the grand coalition will be the ruling coalition and conditions under
2:44:3066:14:14:72:540:322:12:Times:12:Times:F:which the most powerful individuals will not be included in the ruling coalition.  We also use this
2:45:3165:14:28:72:316:308:12:Times:12:Times:F:framework to discuss endogenous party formation.
2:46:3213:28:14:72:155:280:12:Times:12:Times:F:Daron Acemoglu
2:47:3227:14:14:72:198:266:12:Times:12:Times:F:Department of Economics
2:48:3250:14:14:72:149:252:12:Times:12:Times:F:MIT, E52-380B
2:49:3263:14:14:72:165:238:12:Times:12:Times:F:50 Memorial Drive
2:50:3280:14:14:72:215:224:12:Times:12:Times:F:Cambridge, MA  02142-1347
2:51:3305:14:14:72:124:210:12:Times:12:Times:F:and NBER
2:52:3313:14:28:72:147:196:12:Times:12:Times:F:daron@mit.edu
2:53:3326:28:14:72:146:168:12:Times:12:Times:F:Georgy Egorov
2:54:3339:14:14:72:145:154:12:Times:12:Times:F:Littauer Center
2:55:3354:14:14:72:183:140:12:Times:12:Times:F:1805 Cambridge Street

2:57:3394:14:0:72:196:112:12:Times:12:Times:F:gegorov@fas.harvard.edu
2:58:3417:0:14:306:390:280:12:Times:12:Times:F:Konstantin Sonin
2:59:3433:14:14:306:417:266:12:Times:12:Times:F:New Economic School
2:60:3452:14:14:306:421:252:12:Times:12:Times:F:47 Nakhimovsky prosp.

3:63:3508:0:30:72:201:714:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:1Introduction
3:64:3521:30:20:72:539:684:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Consider a society in which each individual possesses some amount of military power (“guns”) and
3:65:3617:20:20:72:539:664:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:can form a “coalition” with other individuals tofight against the remaining individuals. A group
3:66:3713:20:20:72:539:644:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(coalition) that has sufficient power becomes the “ruling coalition”; it determines the allocation of
3:67:3814:20:20:72:540:624:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:resources in the society, e.g., how a pie of size 1 will be distributed. A group with more guns can
3:68:3913:20:20:72:540:604:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:eliminate (win against) a group with less guns. However, once the elimination has taken place, a
3:69:4009:20:19:72:539:584:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:subgroup within the winning group can engage in further rounds of eliminations in order to reduce
3:70:4106:19:20:72:540:565:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the size of the ruling coalition and receive more for each of its members. What types of ruling
3:71:4201:20:20:72:539:545:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions do we expect to form? Will there generally be multiple “equilibrium” or “stable” ruling
3:72:4299:20:20:72:473:525:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions? Will more powerful individuals necessarily obtain more of the resources?
3:73:4383:20:20:88:539:505:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Consider an alternative scenario in which a group of individuals needs to form a committee to
3:74:4476:20:20:72:540:485:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:reach a decision. A group that has a (power-weighted) majority can impose the selection of a par-
3:75:4573:20:20:72:539:465:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ticular committee, thus potentially influencing the collective choice. However, once the committee
3:76:4671:20:19:72:540:445:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:forms, a subgroup within the committee may sideline some of the members and impose its own
3:77:4761:19:20:72:345:426:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:rule. What types of committees do we expect to emerge?
3:78:4815:20:20:88:539:406:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The key feature in both of these examples is that the structure and nature of the ruling coalition
3:79:4913:20:20:72:539:386:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:depends not only the power of different groups (coalitions), but also whether, once formed, a
3:80:5006:20:20:71:539:366:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:particular group will be stable, i.e.,self-enforcing. This tension between the power and the stability
3:81:5108:20:20:71:539:346:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of a group is a common feature in many situations where coalitions have to form in order to make
3:82:5204:20:19:71:347:326:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:collective choices or determine the allocation of resources.
3:83:5264:19:20:88:539:307:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:To investigate these questions systematically, we consider a society consisting of afinite number
3:84:5361:20:20:71:539:287:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of individuals, each with an exogenously given level of political power.1A group’s power is the sum
3:85:5460:20:20:72:539:267:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of the power of its members. The society has afixed resource, e.g., a pie of size 1. The distribution
3:86:5561:20:20:72:548:247:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of this resource among the individualsis determined by a (self-enforcing)ruling coalition.For
3:87:5654:20:20:71:539:227:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:concreteness, let us suppose that aruling coalition distributes this resource among its members
3:88:5749:20:20:71:539:207:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:according to their political power. A ruling coalition needs to satisfy two requirements. First, it
3:89:5848:20:19:71:539:187:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:needs to have total power more thanα∈[1/2,1)times the power of all the individuals in society,
3:90:5942:19:20:72:539:168:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:so that it is awinningcoalition. This is captured by thepower constraint. Second, it should have
3:91:6038:20:20:71:539:148:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:no subcoalition that would be willing to secede and become the new ruling coalition, so that it is
3:92:6136:20:20:71:509:128:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:self-enforcing or stable. This second requirement is captured by theenforcement constraint.
3:93:6227:20:16:88:539:108:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:We show that a subcoalition will be self-enforcing if its own winning subcoalitions are not self-
3:94:6324:16:15:84:539:92:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:1Throughout, we will work with a society consisting of individuals. Groups that have solved their internal collective
3:95:6441:15:0:72:512:77:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:action problem and have well-defined preferences can be considered as equivalent to individuals in this game.
4:96:6551:0:20:72:540:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing. Intuitively, any subcoalition that is both winning and self-enforcing will secede from the
4:97:6652:20:19:72:540:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:original coalition and obtain more for its members. Subcoalitions that are not self-enforcing will
4:98:6750:19:20:72:540:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:prefer not to secede because some of their members will realize that they will be left out of the
4:99:6847:20:20:72:402:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ultimate ruling coalition at the next round of secession (elimination).
4:100:6918:20:20:88:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:One of the simple but interesting implications of these interactions is that under majority rule,
4:101:7015:20:20:72:540:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ruling coalitions are generically (in a sense to be made precise below) not two-person coalitions,
4:102:7113:20:32:72:369:595:121:g_d0_f5:65:g_d0_f2:C:duumvirates, but can be three-person coalitions,triumvirates.2
4:103:7175:32:19:72:539:563:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Example 1Consider two agentsAandBwith powersγA>0andγB>0and assume that the
4:104:7249:19:20:72:544:544:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:decision-making rule requires power-weighted majority (i.e.,α=1/2). IfγA>γB,thenstarting
4:105:7337:20:20:71:539:524:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:with a coalition of agentsAandB,theagentAwill form a majority by himself. Conversely, if
4:106:7425:20:20:71:539:504:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:γA<γB, then agentBwill form a majority. Thus, “generically” (i.e., as long asγA6=γB), one of
4:107:7517:20:20:71:539:484:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the members of the two-person coalition can secede and form a subcoalition that is powerful enough
4:108:7615:20:20:71:539:464:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:within the original coalition. Since each agent will receive a higher share of the scarce resources in a
4:109:7719:20:20:71:539:444:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalition that consists of only himself than in a two-person coalition, such a coalition, a duumvirate,
4:110:7822:20:19:71:221:424:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:is generically not self-enforcing.
4:111:7856:19:20:88:539:405:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Now, consider a coalition consisting of three agents,A,BandCwith powersγA,γBandγC,
4:112:7938:20:20:72:539:385:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and suppose thatγA<γB<γC<γA+γB. Clearly no two-person coalition is self-enforcing.
4:113:8020:20:20:72:539:365:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:The lack of self-enforcing subcoalitions of(A,B,C), in turn, implies that(A,B,C)is itself self-
4:114:8115:20:20:72:539:345:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing.  To see this, suppose, for example, that a subcoalition of(A,B,C),(A,B)considers
4:115:8206:20:20:72:547:325:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:seceding from the original coalition.  They can do so sinceγA+γB>γC.However,weknow
4:116:8288:20:19:71:539:305:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:from the previous paragraph that the subcoalition(A,B)is itself not self-enforcing, since after
4:117:8383:19:20:71:539:286:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f6:B:this coalition is established, agentBwould secede or “eliminate”A. Anticipating this, agentA
4:118:8475:20:20:71:539:266:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:would not support the subcoalition(A,B). A similar argument applies for all other subcoalitions.
4:119:8571:20:20:71:539:246:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Moreover, since agentCis not powerful enough to secede from the original coalition by himself,
4:120:8665:20:20:71:540:226:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the three-person coalition(A,B,C)is self-enforcing.  Consequently, a triumvirate can be self-
4:121:8758:20:20:71:539:206:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing and become the ruling coalition. This example also shows that contrary to approaches
4:122:8852:20:20:71:540:186:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:with unrestricted side-payments (e.g., Riker, 1962), the ruling coalition will not generally be the
4:123:8951:20:19:71:360:166:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:minimal winning coalition (which is(A,B)in this example).
4:124:9008:19:20:88:539:147:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Next, consider a society consisting of four individuals. To illustrate the main ideas, suppose
4:125:9102:20:20:71:539:127:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:that we haveγA=3,γB=4,γC=5as well as an additional individual,D,withpowerγD=10.
4:126:9181:20:17:71:539:107:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:D’s power is insufficient to eliminate the coalition(A,B,C)starting from the initial coalition
4:127:9275:17:14:84:539:90:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:2Duumvirate and triumvirate are, respectively, the terms given to two-man and three-man executive bodies in
4:128:9382:14:0:72:132:76:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:Ancient Rome.
5:129:9396:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f2:B:(A,B,C,D). Nevertheless,Dis stronger than any two ofA,B,C. This implies that any three-
5:130:9483:20:19:72:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:B:person coalition that includesDwould not be self-enforcing. Anticipating this, any two of(A,B,C)
5:131:9579:19:20:71:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:would resistD’s offer to secede and eliminate the third. However,(A,B,C)is self-enforcing, thus
5:132:9674:20:20:71:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the three agents would be happy to eliminateD. Therefore, in this example, the ruling coalition
5:133:9769:20:20:71:519:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:again consists of three individuals, but interestingly excludes the most powerful individualD.
5:134:9863:20:20:88:540:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:A:The most powerful individual is not always eliminated. Consider the society withγA=2,γB=
5:135:9951:20:20:72:539:595:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f2:B:4,γC=7andγD=10. In this case, among the three-person coalitions only(B,C,D)is self-
5:136:10034:20:30:72:539:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing, thusB,CandDwill eliminate the weakest individual,A, and become the ruling coalition.
5:137:10129:30:20:88:539:545:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:This example highlights the central roles of the power and the enforcement constraints, which
5:138:10222:20:20:72:549:525:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:are illustrated diagrammatically in Figure 1 for a society with three members,(A,B,C).The
5:139:10311:20:20:72:539:505:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:two dimensional simplex in thefigure represents the powers of the three players (with their sum
5:140:10406:20:19:72:539:485:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:normalized to 1 without loss of generality). The shaded area in thefirst panel is the set of all
5:141:10502:19:20:72:540:466:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions where the subcoalition(A,B)is winning and shows the power constraint, which is parallel
5:142:10600:20:158:72:225:446:121:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:to theABfacet of the simplex.3
5:143:10630:158:20:156:471:288:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The Power ConstraintThe Enforcement Constraint
5:144:10676:20:41:282:328:268:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f1:C:Figure 1
5:145:10684:41:20:88:539:227:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The enforcement constraint (for a subcoalition), on the other hand, defines the area, where, if
5:146:10779:20:20:71:539:207:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:other players are eliminated, the subcoalition still remains self-enforcing. The second panel depicts
5:147:10880:20:20:71:539:187:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the enforcement constraint for the subcoalition(A,B)when playerCis eliminated for a game with
5:148:10973:20:20:71:539:167:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:α>1/2.When|N|=3,the enforcement constraint defines a cone.4Inthecasewhereα=1/2,
5:149:11052:20:15:72:379:147:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:this cone becomes a straight line perpendicular to theABfacet.
5:150:11114:15:15:84:539:132:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:3More generally, ifXis a coalition in a societyN, then its power constraint corresponds to a hyperplane in a
5:151:11222:15:11:72:540:117:82:g_d0_f12:82:g_d0_f2:F:(|N|−1)-dimensional simplex, which is parallel to a(|X|−1)-dimensional facet that contains all vertices fromX,
5:152:11332:11:7:72:361:106:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:and to a(|N|−|X|−1)-dimensional facet containing all other vertices.
5:153:11400:7:15:84:540:99:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:4More generally, forN>3and a proper coalitionX, the enforcement constraint defines a quasi-cone, that is, a
5:154:11507:15:11:72:540:84:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:union of all segments that connect any point from the(|N|−|X|−1)-dimensional facet containing all vertices from
5:155:11618:11:0:72:501:73:82:g_d0_f11:82:g_d0_f2:F:N\Xto the set of self-enforcing points on the(|X|−1)-dimensional facet containing all vertices fromX.
6:156:11720:0:20:88:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:A:Using thisfigure, we can determine the distributionsof powers for which the subcoalition(A,B)
6:157:11813:20:19:71:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:can emerge as the ruling coalition within(A,B,C). First, it needs to be powerful enough, i.e., lie
6:158:11911:19:20:72:540:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:in the shaded area in thefirst panel. Second, it needs to be self-enforcing, i.e., lie in the cone of
6:159:12012:20:20:72:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcement in the second panel. Clearly, whenα=1/2, only a segment of the line where the
6:160:12101:20:20:72:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:powers ofAandBare equal can satisfy these constraints, which captures the result in Example
6:161:12192:20:20:72:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:1 that, generically, a two-person coalition cannot become a ruling coalition under majority rule.
6:162:12289:20:20:72:539:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:More generally, a coalitionXcan threaten the stability of the grand coalition only if both the
6:163:12383:20:20:71:320:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:power and the enforcement constraints are satisfied.
6:164:12435:20:19:88:539:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Ourfirst major result is that an axiomatic approach to the determination of the ruling coalition
6:165:12531:19:20:71:539:536:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:using these two notions, together with two other technical axioms, is sufficient to single out a unique
6:166:12634:20:20:71:539:516:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ruling coalition in generic games. We achieve this by defining a mapping from the set of coalitions
6:167:12733:20:20:71:539:496:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of the society into itself that satisfies the above-mentioned axioms. When applied to the entire
6:168:12829:20:20:71:296:476:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:society, this mapping gives theruling coalition.
6:169:12877:20:20:88:539:456:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:That this axiomatic approach and the notion of ruling coalition capture important aspects of the
6:170:12973:20:19:71:539:436:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:process of coalition formation in political gamesis reinforced by our analysis of a simple dynamic
6:171:13071:19:20:71:539:417:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:game of coalition formation. In particular, we consider a dynamic game where at each stage a
6:172:13163:20:20:71:539:397:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:subset of the agents forms a coalition and “eliminates” those outside the coalition. The game ends
6:173:13261:20:20:71:539:377:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:when an ultimate ruling coalition, which does not wish to engage in further elimination, emerges.
6:174:13358:20:20:71:539:357:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:This ultimate ruling coalition divides the resources among its members according to their power.
6:175:13454:20:20:71:539:337:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:The important assumptions here are as follows. First, a player who is eliminated at any point
6:176:13547:20:19:71:539:317:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:cannot join future coalitions. This is in line with the motivating examples given above. Second,
6:177:13643:19:20:71:539:298:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:there is no possibility of commitment to the division of the resources once the ruling coalition is
6:178:13742:20:20:71:539:278:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:established. This no-commitment assumption is natural in political games, since it is impossible to
6:179:13841:20:20:71:539:258:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:make commitments or write contracts on future political decisions.5We establish the existence and
6:180:13938:20:20:72:540:238:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:generic uniqueness of sequentially weakly dominant and Markov trembling hand perfect equilibria
6:181:14033:20:20:72:539:218:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of this dynamic game.6We also show that these equilibrium outcomes coincide with the ruling
6:182:14124:20:16:72:295:198:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalition derived from the axiomatic approach.
6:183:14170:16:14:84:540:182:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:5See Acemoglu and Robinson (2006) for a discussion. Browne and Franklin (1973), Browne and Frendreis (1980),
6:184:14278:14:11:72:539:168:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:Schoffield and Laver (1985), and Warwick and Druckman (2001) provide empirical evidence consistent with the notion
6:185:14392:11:11:72:540:157:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:that ruling coalitions share resources according to thepowers of their members. For example, these papersfind a
6:186:14503:11:11:72:539:146:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:linear relationship between parties’ shares of parliamentary seats (a proxy for their political power) and their shares
6:187:14622:11:11:72:539:135:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:of cabinet positions (“their share of the pie”). Ansolabehere et al. (2005)find a similar relationship between cabinet
6:188:14740:11:11:72:540:124:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:positions and voting weights (which are even more closely related to political power in our model) and note that:
6:189:14853:11:11:72:539:113:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:“The relationship is so strong and robust that some researchers call it ‘Gamson’s Law’ (after Gamson, 1961, who was
6:190:14968:11:7:72:236:102:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:thefirst to predict such a relationship).”
6:191:15010:7:15:84:540:95:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:6In fact, we establish the more general result that allagenda-setting games(as defined below) have a sequentially
6:192:15123:15:0:72:396:80:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:weakly dominant equilibrium and a Markov trembling hand perfect equilibrium.
7:193:15200:0:20:88:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, we show that the same solution emerges when we model the process of coalition forma-
7:194:15293:20:19:71:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:tion as a non-transferable utility cooperative game incorporating the notion that only self-enforcing
7:195:15394:19:20:71:443:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions can implement allocations that give high payoffstotheirmembers.
7:196:15468:20:20:88:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:At some level, it may not be surprising that all these approaches lead to the same result,
7:197:15558:20:20:71:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:since they capture the same salient features of the process of collective decision-making–the power
7:198:15657:20:20:71:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and the enforcement constraints. Nevertheless,the three approaches model these features in very
7:199:15752:20:20:71:497:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:different ways. We thereforefind it reassuring that they all lead to the same conclusions.
7:200:15842:20:31:88:500:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Our substantive results relate to the structure of ruling coalitions in this environment:
7:201:15931:31:20:85:539:544:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:1. There always exists a ruling coalition andit can be computed by induction on the number of
7:202:16024:20:29:99:135:524:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:players.
7:203:16032:29:20:85:539:495:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:2. Despite the simplicity of the environment, the ruling coalition can consist of any number of
7:204:16127:20:20:99:539:475:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:players, and may include or exclude the most powerful individuals in the society.  Conse-
7:205:16216:20:29:99:476:455:121:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:A:quently, the equilibrium payoffof an individual is not monotonic in his power.7
7:206:16295:29:19:85:539:426:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:3. Relatedly, the most powerful individual will be excluded from the ruling coalition, unless he
7:207:16391:19:20:99:539:407:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:is powerful enough to win by himself or weak enough so as to be part of smaller self-enforcing
7:208:16485:20:29:99:147:387:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:coalitions.
7:209:16496:29:20:85:540:358:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:4. Again somewhat paradoxically, an increase inα, i.e., an increase in the degree of superma-
7:210:16589:20:20:99:539:338:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:jority, does not necessarily lead to larger ruling coalitions, because it stabilizes otherwise
7:211:16683:20:20:99:539:318:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:non-self-enforcing subcoalitions, and as a result, destroys larger coalitions that would have
7:212:16776:20:28:99:291:298:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:been self-enforcing for lower values ofα.
7:213:16817:28:20:85:539:270:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:5. Self-enforcing coalitions are generally “fragile.” For example, under majority rule, i.e.,
7:214:16910:20:20:99:539:250:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:A:α=1/2, adding or subtracting one player from a self-enforcing coalition makes it non-
7:215:16995:20:29:99:164:230:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:self-enforcing.
7:216:17010:29:20:85:539:201:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:6. Nevertheless,rulingcoalitions are (generically) continuous in the distribution of power across
7:217:17107:20:20:99:539:181:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:individuals in the sense that a ruling coalition remains so when the powers of the players are
7:218:17201:20:28:99:242:161:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:perturbed by a small amount.
7:219:17229:28:20:85:540:133:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:7. Coalitions of certain sizes are more likely to emerge as the ruling coalition. For example, with
7:220:17328:20:17:99:539:113:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:majority rule, the ruling coalition cannot (generically) consist of two individuals. Moreover,
7:221:17422:17:15:84:539:96:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:7In terms of ourfirst motivating example, this implies that individuals may wish to “give up their guns” voluntarily
7:222:17538:15:0:72:539:81:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:as a “commitment” not to overpower members of certain coalitions and thus be accepted as part of these coalitions.
8:223:17653:0:20:99:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:again under majority rule, coalitions where members have relatively equal powers are self-
8:224:17743:20:31:99:436:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:enforcing only when the coalition’s size is2k−1wherekis an integer.
8:225:17810:31:20:88:539:663:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Our paper is related to a number of different literatures. Thefirst is the social choice litera-
8:226:17906:20:20:71:539:643:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ture. The difficulty of determining the social welfare function of a society highlighted by Arrow’s
8:227:18005:20:20:71:540:623:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(im)possibility theorem is related to the fact that the core of the game defined over the allocation of
8:228:18108:20:20:71:539:603:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:resources is empty (Arrow, 1951, Austen-Smith and Banks, 1999). Our approach therefore focuses
8:229:18202:20:20:71:539:583:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:on a weaker notion than the core, whereby only “self-enforcing” coalitions are allowed to form. Our
8:230:18301:20:19:71:540:563:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:paper therefore contributes to the collective choice literature by considering a different notion of
8:231:18401:19:20:71:475:544:121:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:aggregating individual preferences and establishes that such aggregation is possible.8
8:232:18487:20:20:88:539:524:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Our work is also related to models of bargaining over resources, both generally and in the
8:233:18577:20:20:71:539:504:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:context of political decision-making. In political economy (collective choice) context, two different
8:234:18678:20:20:71:539:484:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:approaches are worth noting. Thefirst is given by the legislative bargaining models (e.g., Baron
8:235:18774:20:20:71:539:464:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and Ferejohn, 1989, Calvert and Dietz, 1996, Jackson and Boaz, 2002), which characterize the
8:236:18866:20:20:71:539:444:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes of bargaining among a set of players by assuming specific game-forms approximating the
8:237:18961:20:19:71:539:424:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:legislative bargaining process in practice. Our approach differs from this strand of the literature,
8:238:19061:19:20:71:539:405:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:sincewedonotimposeanyspecific bargaining structure. The second strand includes Shapley and
8:239:19151:20:20:71:539:385:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Shubik (1954) on power struggles in committees and the paper by Aumann and Kurz (1977), which
8:240:19244:20:20:71:539:365:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:looks at the Shapley value of a bargaining game to determine the distribution of resources in the
8:241:19341:20:20:71:540:345:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:society.9Our approach is different since we focus on the endogenously-emerging ruling coalition
8:242:19436:20:20:72:540:325:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:rather than bargaining among the entire set ofagents in a society or in an exogenously-formed
8:243:19529:20:19:72:125:305:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:committee.
8:244:19539:19:20:88:539:286:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:At a more abstract level, our approach is a contribution to the literature on equilibrium coalition
8:245:19638:20:20:72:540:266:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:formation, which combines elements from both cooperative and noncooperative game theory (e.g.,
8:246:19732:20:20:72:540:246:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Peleg, 1980, Hart and Kurz, 1983, Aumann and Myerson, 1988, Greenberg and Weber, 1993,
8:247:19818:20:20:72:540:226:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Chwe, 1994, Bloch, 1996, Ray and Vohra, 1997, 1999, 2001, Seidmann and Winter, 1998, Konishi
8:248:19910:20:16:72:539:206:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and Ray, 2001, Maskin, 2003).10Themostimportantdifference between our approach and the
8:249:19996:16:15:84:539:190:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:8In this respect, our paper is also related to work on “coalition-proof” Nash equilibrium or rationalizability,
8:250:20107:15:11:72:540:175:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:e.g., Bernheim, Peleg and Whinston (1987), Moldovanu (1992), Ambrus (2006). These papers allow deviations by
8:251:20215:11:11:72:540:164:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:coalitions in non-cooperative games, but imposethat only stable coalitions can form. The main difference is that
8:252:20327:11:11:72:540:153:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:our basic approach is axiomatic or cooperative. We then provide a non-cooperative foundation for our approach,
8:253:20437:11:11:72:539:142:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:but do not explicitly use coalition-proofness as a refinement in the non-cooperative game.  Another difference is
8:254:20550:11:11:72:539:131:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:that coalition-proof Nash equilibria typically fail to exist (though coalitionally rationalizable outcomes do exist, see
8:255:20670:11:11:72:540:120:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:Ambrus, 2006), while we show existence and generic uniqueness of our equilibrium concept in all three approaches
8:256:20782:11:7:72:111:109:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:we adopt.
8:257:20791:7:15:84:539:102:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:9See also the literature on weighted majority cooperative games, which also model situations in which different
8:258:20902:15:7:72:526:87:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:individuals have different “weights” or “powers,” e.g., Isbell (1956), Peleg (1968), Peleg and Rosenmuller (1992).
8:259:21016:7:0:80:540:80:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:10Like some of these papers, our approach can be situated within the “Nash program” since our axiomatic approach
9:260:21129:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:previous literature on coalition formation is that, motivated by political settings, we assume that
9:261:21228:20:19:72:540:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the majority (or supermajority) of the members of the society can impose their will on those
9:262:21320:19:20:72:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:players who are not a part of the majority.11This feature both changes the nature of the game
9:263:21413:20:20:71:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and also introduces “negative externalities” as opposed to the positive externalities and free-rider
9:264:21513:20:20:71:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:problems upon which the previous literature focuses (see, for example, Ray and Vohra, 1999, and
9:265:21608:20:20:71:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Maskin, 2003). A second important difference is that most of these works assume the possibility
9:266:21703:20:20:71:539:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of binding commitments (see again Ray and Vohra, 1997, 1999), while we suppose that players
9:267:21794:20:20:71:539:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:have no commitment power. In addition, many previous approaches have proposed equilibrium
9:268:21883:20:19:71:539:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:concepts for cooperative games by restricting the set of coalitions that can block an allocation.
9:269:21980:19:20:71:540:536:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Myerson (1991, ch. 9) and Osborne and Rubinstein(1994, ch. 14) give comprehensive discussions
9:270:22073:20:20:71:539:516:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of many of these approaches. Our paper is also a contribution to this literature, since we propose a
9:271:22173:20:20:71:539:496:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:different axiomatic solution concept. To the best of our knowledge, neither the axiomatic approach
9:272:22271:20:20:71:543:476:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:nor the specificcooperativegameformnorthedynamicgameweanalyzeinthispaperhavebeen
9:273:22351:20:20:71:496:456:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:considered in the previous literatures on cooperative game theory or coalition formation.
9:274:22440:20:19:88:539:436:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The rest of the paper is organized as follows. Section 2 introduces the basic political game and
9:275:22536:19:20:71:539:417:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:contains a brief discussion of why it captures certain salient features of political decision-making.
9:276:22637:20:20:71:539:397:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Section 3 provides our axiomatic treatment of this game.  It introduces the concept of ruling
9:277:22730:20:20:71:539:377:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalition and proves its existence and generic uniqueness. Section 4 considers a dynamic game of
9:278:22826:20:20:71:539:357:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalition formation and a number of equilibrium concepts for this type of extensive-form games. It
9:279:22924:20:20:71:539:337:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:then establishes the equivalence between the ruling coalition of Section 3 and the equilibria of this
9:280:23025:20:19:71:539:317:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:extensive-form game. Section 5 introduces the cooperative game and establishes the equivalence
9:281:23119:19:20:71:539:298:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:between the core allocations of this game and the ruling coalitions. Section 6 contains our main
9:282:23215:20:20:71:539:278:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:results on the nature and structure of ruling coalitions in political games. Section 7 considers a
9:283:23313:20:20:71:539:258:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:number of extensions such as endogenous party formation and voluntary redistribution of power
9:284:23406:20:20:71:539:238:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:within a coalition. Section 8 concludes, and the Appendices contain the proofs not provided in the
9:285:23504:20:20:71:507:218:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:text as well as a number of examples to further motivate some of our equilibrium concepts.
9:286:23594:20:11:72:539:198:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:is supported by an explicit extensive form game (Nash,1953). See Serrano (2005) for a recent survey of work on the
9:287:23708:11:7:72:132:187:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:Nash program.
9:288:23721:7:14:80:539:180:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:11This is a distinctive and general feature of political games. In presidential systems, the political contest is winner-
9:289:23842:14:11:72:540:166:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:take-all by design, while in parliamentary systems, parties left out of the governing coalition typically have limited
9:290:23960:11:0:72:360:155:82:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:say over political decisions. The same is a fortiori true in dictatorships.
10:291:24036:0:30:72:250:714:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2ThePoliticalGame
10:292:24053:30:20:72:539:684:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:We are interested in coalition-formation among afinite set of individuals. LetIbe a collection

11:327:26340:20:20:88:540:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:A:Given this description, for any societyNwe definean abstract political gameas a tripleΓ=

11:345:27625:31:20:88:539:254:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The restrictions onwi(X)are quite natural and capture the idea that the player’s payoffs depend
11:346:27720:20:20:71:540:234:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:positively on the player’s relative strength in theruling coalition. The most important assumption
11:347:27818:20:20:71:540:214:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:introduced so far is that a coalition cannot commit to an arbitrary distribution of resources among
11:348:27917:20:20:71:539:194:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:its members. Instead, the allocation of resources is determined by the payofffunctions{wi(·)}i∈N.
11:349:28014:20:20:72:540:174:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:For example, a coalition consisting of two individuals with powers1and10cannot commit to share
11:350:28108:20:19:72:540:154:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the resource equally if it becomes the ruling coalition. This assumption will play an important
11:351:28203:19:20:72:540:135:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:role in our analysis. We view this as the essence ofpolitical-economic decision-making: political
11:352:28300:20:20:72:540:115:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:decisions are made by whichever group has political power at the time, and ex ante commitments
11:353:28394:20:20:72:539:95:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:to future political decisions are generally not possible (see the discussion and references in footnote
11:354:28497:20:0:72:85:75:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:5).

12:380:29692:20:20:88:539:329:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:We will sometimes impose the following assumption to obtain sharper results (though this

13:391:30532:0:30:72:233:714:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3  Axiomatic Analysis
13:392:30553:30:20:72:539:684:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:We begin with an axiomatic analysis. Our approach is to impose some natural restrictions on the
13:393:30648:20:20:72:540:664:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:outcome mappingΦthat capture the salient features related to the formation of ruling coalitions.
13:394:30744:20:20:72:539:644:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:In particular, we would like the outcome mapping todetermine the ruling coalitions for an arbitrary
13:395:30843:20:20:72:539:624:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:society. Such a ruling coalition must be winning (according to Definition 1) and self-enforcing, i.e.
13:396:30944:20:20:72:540:604:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:must be able to withstand challenges from its subcoalitions that satisfy the enforcement constraint
13:397:31043:20:19:71:299:584:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(i.e., from subcoalitions that are self-enforcing).
13:398:31094:19:20:88:543:565:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Let usfix an abstract gameΓ(N,γ|N,α), that is, a power mappingγ:I→R++,aparameter
13:399:31174:20:30:71:381:545:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:α∈[1/2,1),andasocietyN∈P(I).Define the correspondence
13:400:31227:30:29:263:347:515:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f8:C:φ:P(I)⇒P(I)
13:401:31238:29:20:72:540:486:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:byφ(N)=Φ(Γ(N,γ|N,α))for anyN∈P(I).Wewilluseφinstead ofΦwhenever this causes
13:402:31313:20:20:71:134:466:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:no confusion.
13:403:31326:20:20:88:539:446:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Fix an abstract gameΓ=(N,γ,α).  Then in the spirit of the power and the enforcement
13:404:31409:20:31:71:303:426:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:constraints, we adopt the following axioms onφ.
13:405:31456:31:30:71:487:395:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Axiom 1(Inclusion)For anyX∈P(N),φ(X)6=∅and ifY∈φ(X)thenY⊂X.
13:406:31515:30:31:71:398:365:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Axiom 2(Power)For anyX∈P(N)andY∈φ(X),γY>αγX.
13:407:31559:31:30:71:431:334:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Axiom 3(Enforcement)For anyX∈P(N)andY∈φ(X),Y∈φ(Y).
13:408:31609:30:20:72:539:304:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Axiom 4(Group Rationality)For anyX∈P(N), for anyY∈φ(X)and anyZ⊂Xsuch
13:409:31677:20:31:72:412:284:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:thatγZ>αγXandZ∈φ(Z),wehavethatZ/∈φ(X)⇐⇒γY<γZ.
13:410:31722:31:19:88:539:253:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Motivated by Axiom 3, we define the notion of a self-enforcing coalition as a coalition that
13:411:31814:19:31:71:433:234:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:“selects itself”. This notion will be used repeatedly in the rest of the paper.
13:412:31893:31:31:71:383:203:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Definition 2CoalitionX∈P(I)isself-enforcingifX∈φ(X).
13:413:31945:31:19:88:539:172:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:All four axioms are natural. Axiom 1, inclusion, implies thatφmaps into subcoalitions of the
13:414:32037:19:20:71:540:153:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalition it operates upon and that it is defined, i.e.,φ(X)6=∅.(Note that this does not rule
13:415:32130:20:20:71:539:133:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:outφ(X)={∅}, which is instead ruled out by Axiom 2.) Intuitively, this axiom implies that
13:416:32219:20:20:71:539:113:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:new players cannot join a coalition, which is the key feature of the political game we study in
13:417:32314:20:20:71:539:93:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:this paper. Axiom 2, the power axiom, requires that the winning coalition lies withinXand has
13:418:32407:20:0:71:539:73:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:sufficient power according to Definition 1. Axiom 3, the enforcement axiom, simply requires that
14:419:32505:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:any coalitionY∈φ(X)(for someX∈P(N)) should be self-enforcing according to Definition 2.
14:420:32592:20:19:72:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Axiom 4 requires that if two coalitionsY,Z⊂Xare winning and self-enforcing and all players in

14:422:32768:20:20:72:540:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:an individual rationality or “group rationality” type axiom: sinceα≥1/2, any two winning self-
14:423:32862:20:20:72:540:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing coalitions intersect, and we merely require players from such intersection to have rational
14:424:32963:20:20:72:540:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:preferences between these two coalitions (recall thatwi(·)is such that playeriprefers a coalition

23:881:53832:20:20:71:543:133:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium (see, e.g., Theorem 6). Second, the SWDE URC coincides withφ(N),thatis,withthe

23:883:54015:20:20:72:540:93:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:allows us to use the inductive algorithm to determine the URC of the dynamic game. Finally, when
23:884:54111:20:0:72:345:73:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Assumption 1 holds, the URC is the same in all SWDEs.
24:885:54166:0:20:88:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:While the equivalence between pure strategy SWDE and our axiomatic approach is reassur-
24:886:54253:20:19:72:540:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ing, in Appendix A, we introduce the concept of Markov Trembling-Hand Perfect Equilibrium
24:887:54342:19:20:72:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(MTHPE), which is a slight refinement of the standard Trembling-Hand Perfect Equilibrium. We
24:888:54434:20:20:72:540:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:then prove that the same results apply with MTHPE as well. In this process, we also establish a
24:889:54529:20:20:72:540:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:number of more general results about the existence and structure of MTHPE in a broad class of
24:890:54622:20:34:72:342:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:agenda-setting games, which are of independent interest.
24:891:54678:34:31:72:246:581:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:5  A Cooperative Game
24:892:54699:31:20:72:540:550:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:In this section, we present a non-transferableutility cooperative game and establish that the
24:893:54792:20:20:72:540:530:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(strong) core of this game coincides with the ruling coalition derived in Section 3.14This ex-
24:894:54886:20:20:72:540:510:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ercise is useful both because it links our equilibrium concept to those in the cooperative game
24:895:54981:20:19:72:540:490:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:theory literature and also because it provides another justification for our axiomatic approach. It
24:896:55080:19:20:72:540:471:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:is noteworthy that while the cooperative game theory approach is related to the axiomatic approach
24:897:55178:20:20:72:539:451:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:in Section 3, there are also crucial differences. First, the axiomatic approach involves no strategic
24:898:55279:20:20:71:544:431:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:interactions; in contrast (and similar to our noncooperativeapproachinSection4),theemphasis
24:899:55370:20:20:71:539:411:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:here will be on strategic interactions among players and how there emerges a coalition structure
24:900:55466:20:20:71:539:391:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:implementing a payoffallocation such that no other coalition can implement an alternative feasible
24:901:55564:20:19:71:539:371:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:allocation making all of its members better off. Second, the cooperative approach incorporates the
24:902:55662:19:20:71:393:352:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:dynamic interactions that were also present in the previous section.
24:903:55730:20:31:88:543:332:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:A non-transferable utility cooperative game is represented by ̃ΓN= ̃Γ(N,γ|N,α,vN(·)),where
24:904:55820:31:31:261:344:301:121:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f17:C:vN:P(N)⇒R|N|+

24:906:55933:20:0:72:318:250:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f6:B:that the range of the mapping is notR|N|+, butP
24:907:55980:0:12:321:328:262:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:³

24:910:55988:12:20:355:539:250:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:, since typically a given coalition can
24:911:56027:20:19:72:286:230:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforce more than a single vector of utilities.

24:915:56361:20:20:72:374:151:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:i∈N(this can always be achieved by a linear transformation).

25:979:58330:20:20:72:540:133:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:To motivate Definition 9 and the payoffvector in(8), we can reason as follows. Let us suppose
25:980:58423:20:20:71:539:113:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:that the allocation that givesxi=wi(N)to eachi∈Nis the “status quo” allocation. Then, an
25:981:58511:20:20:71:539:93:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:α-majority is needed to overrule this allocation, but1−αvotes are sufficient to keep the status quo.
25:982:58611:20:0:71:539:73:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:That every coalition may enforce allocationxi=0for alli∈Nis a requirement of the standard
26:983:58702:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:definition of non-transferable utility cooperative games. Another requirement is that whenX⊂Y,
26:984:58796:20:19:72:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:we should havevN(X)⊂vN(Y). It is straightforward to check that(8)satisfies both requirements.
26:985:58889:19:20:88:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The most important feature of this non-transferable utility cooperative game is that even a
26:986:58980:20:20:71:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:winning coalition does not have complete discretionover the allocation; instead, it may only choose
26:987:59079:20:20:71:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:a core allocation for some smaller coalitionY, which is in some sense equivalent to excluding
26:988:59172:20:17:71:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the players inN\Yfrom “sharing the pie” and making players inYplay the cooperative game
26:989:59259:17:23:72:540:598:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f2:B: ̃Γ(Y,γ|Y,α,vY(·)).  If an allocation is not in the core of this reduced game, then it cannot be
26:990:59355:23:20:71:539:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:imposed, since coalitionYwould rather choose a different allocation. This feature introduces the
26:991:59451:20:29:71:467:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:dynamic aspect mentioned above in the context of the cooperative game approach.
26:992:59530:29:20:71:539:526:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Example 3To illustrate how this game works, consider a society consisting of three individuals
26:993:59624:20:19:71:539:506:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:A,B,Cwith powers(γA,γB,γC)=(3,4,5),letα=1/2. Allocation(3/12,4/12,5/12)is a feasible
26:994:59708:19:20:71:539:487:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:allocation; to see that it is in the core we need to check whether any coalition that has a majority
26:995:59808:20:20:71:539:467:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of votes can improve for all its members. Take, for instance, coalition{B,C}; it is winning and
26:996:59903:20:20:72:539:447:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:therefore can implement any feasible allocation. BothBandCwould be better offif they could
26:997:59993:20:20:72:540:427:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:giveAnothing and share the resource between themselves. However, allocation(0,4/9,5/9)is not
26:998:60085:20:0:72:262:407:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f23:B:feasible because the core of the game ̃Γ
26:999:60125:0:9:264:269:416:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:¡
26:1000:60126:9:0:269:402:407:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f8:C:{B,C},γ|{B,C},α,v{B,C}(·)
26:1001:60151:0:9:402:407:416:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:¢
26:1002:60152:9:20:412:542:407:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:A:is a singleton withxB=0
26:1003:60175:20:20:71:540:387:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:B:andxC=1(Cconstitutes a majority alone and can implement this allocation). Allocation(0,0,1)
26:1004:60266:20:19:72:539:367:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f4:B:is feasible and may be enforced by coalition{B,C}. But, naturally it makes playerBworse off
26:1005:60357:19:20:72:544:348:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:than he would have been with the allocation(3/12,4/12,5/12). Likewisewecanshowthatno
26:1006:60441:20:20:72:539:328:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:other coalition can improve for all its members. Therefore,(3/12,4/12,5/12)is in the core, and it
26:1007:60538:20:29:72:362:308:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:is easy to verify that no other feasible vector lies in the core.
26:1008:60603:29:30:88:249:279:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Our main result in this section is:
26:1009:60638:30:0:72:497:249:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f6:C:Theorem 31. For any ̃ΓN= ̃Γ(N,γ|N,α,vN(·))withvNdefined by(8),thecoreC
26:1010:60708:0:10:499:506:262:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:³
26:1011:60709:10:0:507:520:252:121:g_d0_f8:65:g_d0_f9:C: ̃ΓN
26:1012:60713:0:13:521:528:262:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C: ́
26:1013:60715:13:19:531:539:249:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:is
26:1014:60717:19:28:99:149:230:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:nonempty.
26:1015:60726:28:20:84:539:202:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:2. Take abstract gameΓ(N,γ|N,α)and the outcome setφ(N)corresponding to it (characterized
26:1016:60814:20:0:99:270:182:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f6:C:in Theorem 1). Then, for anyx∈C
26:1017:60845:0:9:272:279:194:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:³
26:1018:60846:9:0:280:293:185:121:g_d0_f8:65:g_d0_f9:C: ̃ΓN
26:1019:60850:0:12:294:301:194:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C: ́

26:1021:60889:20:0:99:357:162:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f6:C:versa, for anyM∈φ(N)there exists a uniquex∈C
26:1022:60933:0:9:360:367:174:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:³

26:1024:60938:0:12:381:388:174:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C: ́

26:1027:61056:20:0:99:328:122:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f6:C:Moreover, when Assumption 1 holds, the coreC
26:1028:61100:0:9:330:337:134:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:³
26:1029:61101:9:0:337:351:125:121:g_d0_f8:65:g_d0_f9:C: ̃ΓN

26:1032:61138:20:29:99:256:102:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f5:C:xthe unique element of the core.
26:1033:61170:29:0:72:190:73:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof.See Appendix C.
27:1034:61193:0:20:88:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:This theorem therefore establishes the equivalence between the axiomatic approach in Section
27:1035:61285:20:19:71:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:3, the dynamic game in the previous section, and the cooperative game in this section, even though
27:1036:61383:19:20:71:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:each of these three different approaches models the determination of the ruling coalition in a
27:1037:61477:20:20:71:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:very different manner. The main idea underlying this result is that only self-enforcing and winning
27:1038:61576:20:20:71:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions can implement payoffvectors that are attractive for their own members. In the framework
27:1039:61674:20:20:71:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of non-transferable utility cooperativegames, this is captured by two features:first, only winning
27:1040:61772:20:20:71:539:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions can implement feasible payoffvectors (Definition 8); second, in addition to zero payoffs
27:1041:61871:20:20:71:539:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and status quo allocation, only payoffvectors that correspond to core allocations for a smaller game
27:1042:61971:20:19:71:539:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:are feasible (Definition 9). These two features introduce the power and enforcement constraints that
27:1043:62071:19:20:71:540:536:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:were also essential in the axiomatic and the dynamic game approaches. In view of this, thefinding
27:1044:62168:20:20:71:539:516:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:that the set of core allocations here correspond to the ruling coalitions is perhaps not surprising,
27:1045:62268:20:34:71:180:496:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:though still reassuring.
27:1046:62292:34:31:72:343:462:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:6  The Structure of Ruling Coalitions
27:1047:62329:31:20:72:540:431:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:In this section, we present several results on the structure of ruling coalitions. Given the equivalence
27:1048:62433:20:20:72:540:411:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:results in the previous two sections, without loss of generality we focus on ruling coalitions of
27:1049:62530:20:32:72:421:391:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:abstract gamesΓ=Γ(N,γ|N,α). In addition to Assumption 1, consider:
27:1050:62596:32:31:72:504:359:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Assumption 2For noX,Y∈P(I)such thatX⊂Ythe equalityγY=αγXis satisfied.
27:1051:62665:31:20:88:536:328:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f6:A:Essentially, Assumption 2 guarantees that a small perturbation of a non-winning coalitionY
27:1052:62755:20:20:72:539:308:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:does not make it winning. Similar to Assumption 1,this assumption fails only in a set of Lebesgue
27:1053:62852:20:20:72:540:288:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:measure 0. Together, Assumptions 1 and 2 simplify the analysis in this section, and we assume
27:1054:62945:20:29:72:529:268:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:that they both hold throughout the section, without explicitly stating this in every proposition.
27:1055:63042:29:27:72:169:239:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:6.1  Robustness
27:1056:63057:27:20:72:540:212:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:We start with the result that the set of self-enforcing coalitions is open (in the standard topology);
27:1057:63159:20:20:72:540:192:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:B:this is not only interesting per se but will facilitate further proofs. Fix a societyNandα∈[1/2,1)

27:1060:63443:20:0:72:364:133:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f23:B:Assumptions 1 and 2 byA(N), the subset ofA(N)for whichΦ

28:1066:63614:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Theorem 41. The set of power allocations that satisfy Assumptions 1 and 2,A(N), its subsets
28:1067:63705:20:19:99:540:694:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:for which coalitionNis self-enforcing,S(N), and its subsets for which coalitionNis not

28:1069:63864:29:29:84:477:646:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:2. Each connected component ofA(N)lies entirely within eitherS(N)orN(N).
28:1070:63936:29:20:72:539:617:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof.(Part 1)The setA(N)may be obtained fromR|N|++by subtracting afinite number of
28:1071:64019:20:20:71:540:597:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:hyperplanes given by equationsγX=γYfor allX,Y∈P(N)such thatX6=Yand by equations

28:1073:64175:20:20:71:539:557:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:standard topology ofR|N|++), hence, a small perturbation of powers of a generic point preserves this
28:1074:64275:20:19:71:539:537:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:property (genericity). This ensures thatA(N)is an open set; it is dense because hyperplanes have
28:1075:64371:19:20:71:539:518:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:dimension lower than|N|. The proofs forS(N)andN(N)are by induction. The base follows
28:1076:64455:20:20:71:540:498:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:immediately sinceS(N)=R++andN(N)=∅are open sets. Now suppose that we have proved
28:1077:64535:20:20:71:539:478:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:this result for allk<|N|.  For any distribution of powers{γi}i∈N,Nis self-enforcing if and
28:1078:64625:20:20:72:540:458:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:only if there are no proper winning self-enforcing coalitions withinN. Now take some small (in
28:1079:64719:20:20:72:539:438:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:sup-metric) perturbation of powers{γ0i}i∈N. If this perturbation is small, then the set of winning
28:1080:64817:20:19:72:539:418:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions is the same, and, by induction, the set of proper self-enforcing coalitions is the same as
28:1081:64918:19:20:72:539:399:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:well. Therefore, the perturbed coalition{γ0i}is self-enforcing if and only if the initial coalition with
28:1082:65022:20:20:71:383:379:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:powers{γi}is self-enforcing; which completes the induction step.
28:1083:65086:20:20:88:540:359:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:(Part 2)Take any connected componentA⊂A(N).BothS(N)∩AandN(N)∩Aare open

28:1086:65309:20:19:71:539:299:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:is connected, implies that eitherS(N)∩AorN(N)∩Ais empty. Hence,Alies either entirely
28:1087:65393:19:20:71:311:280:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:withinS(N)orN(N). This completes the proof.
28:1088:65436:20:20:88:539:260:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:An immediate corollary of Theorem 4 is that if the distribution of powers in two different
28:1089:65526:20:20:71:539:240:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:games are “close,” then these two games will have the same ruling coalition. To state and prove

28:1092:65783:29:30:72:502:171:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 1Fix a societyN,α∈[1/2,1)and a power mappingγ:N→R++.Then:

29:1097:66028:0:20:72:542:714:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f8:C:Proof.We prove this Proposition by induction. IfN=1, it is trivial: for anyγandα,Φ(N,γ,α)=

29:1105:66724:20:19:88:540:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:In addition, we prove that the mappingφis “robust” in the sense that the inclusion of sufficiently

29:1109:67030:32:20:72:539:452:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof.The proof is by induction. Let|N|=n.Forn=1the result follows straightforwardly.

29:1113:67376:20:20:72:539:373:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:obtain a contradiction, assume the contrary, i.e. that the minimal winning self-enforcing coalition
29:1114:67475:20:20:72:545:353:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:X∈P(M∪N)does not coincide withφ(N). Consider its part that lies withinN,X∩N.By

29:1118:67813:19:20:71:539:274:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:However,φ(X∩N)⊂N, and thusX⊂N. Therefore,Xis self-enforcing and winning within

32:1298:73539:20:20:88:539:264:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:A:(Part 4)The proof is by induction. The base is trivial: a one-player coalition is self-enforcing,

33:1322:74563:19:20:88:408:675:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:A:(Part 5)This follows immediately from Part 4 and Proposition 4.
33:1323:74626:20:20:88:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Consequently, while it is impossible to make any general claims about the size of coalitions
33:1324:74718:20:20:71:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:without specifying more details about the distribution of power within the society, we are able
33:1325:74813:20:20:71:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:to provide a tight characterization of the structure of the ruling coalition when individuals are
33:1326:74910:20:29:71:267:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:relatively similar in terms of their power.
33:1327:74953:29:27:72:317:566:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:6.3  Fragility of Self-Enforcing Coalitions
33:1328:74996:27:20:72:540:539:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Here, we show that while the structure of ruling coalitions is robust to small changes in the dis-
33:1329:75094:20:20:72:539:519:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:tribution of power within the society, it may befragile to more sizeable shocks, such as adding or
33:1330:75192:20:19:72:539:499:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:losing a member of the ruling coalition. The next proposition establishes that under simple ma-
33:1331:75287:19:20:72:540:480:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:jority rule, self-enforcing coalitions are fragilein the sense that addition or subtraction of a single
33:1332:75390:20:20:72:539:460:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:agent from these coalitions or, more generally, a unionof two disjoint self-enforcing coalitions leads
33:1333:75492:20:32:72:225:440:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:to a non-self enforcing coalition.
33:1334:75526:32:32:72:458:408:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 6Supposeα=1/2andfix a power mappingγ:I→R++.Then:
33:1335:75586:32:20:84:539:376:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:1. If coalitionsXandYsuch thatX∩Y=∅are both self-enforcing, then coalitionX∪Yis
33:1336:75665:20:28:99:118:356:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:not.
33:1337:75669:28:20:84:539:328:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:2. IfXis a self-enforcing coalition, thenX∪{i}fori/∈XandX\{i}fori∈Xare not
33:1338:75743:20:32:99:165:308:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:self-enforcing.
33:1339:75758:32:20:72:539:276:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof. (Part 1)EitherXis stronger thanYor vice versa. The stronger of the two is a winning
33:1340:75848:20:20:72:539:256:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:self-enforcing coalition that is not equal toX∪Y.ThisimpliesthatX∪Yis not the minimal
33:1341:75933:20:20:72:443:236:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:winning self-enforcing coalition, and so it is not the ruling coalition inX∪Y.
33:1342:76011:20:19:88:539:216:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:A:(Part 2)For the case of adding, it follows directly from Part 1, since coalition of one player is
33:1343:76108:19:20:72:539:197:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:always self-enforcing. For the case of deleting: suppose that it is wrong, and the coalition is self-
33:1344:76209:20:20:72:540:177:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing. Then, by Part 1, adding this person backwill result in an non-self-enforcing coalition.
33:1345:76307:20:29:72:358:157:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:This is a contradiction which completes the proof of Part 2.
33:1346:76367:29:27:72:371:128:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:6.4  Power and the Structure of Ruling Coalitions
33:1347:76416:27:20:72:539:101:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:One might expect that an increase inα–the supermajority requirement–may increase the size
33:1348:76505:20:0:71:539:81:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of the ruling coalition and also turn otherwise non-self-enforcing coalitions into self-enforcing ones
34:1349:76609:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(e.g., coalition(3,4)is not self-enforcing whenα=1/2,but becomes self-enforcing whenα>4/7).
34:1350:76700:20:29:72:277:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Nevertheless, this is generally not the case.
34:1351:76745:29:19:72:540:665:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 7An increase inαmay reduce the size of the ruling coalition. That is, there exists
34:1352:76839:19:20:72:539:646:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f8:C:asocietyN, a power mappingγandα,α0∈[1/2,1), such thatα0>αbut for allX∈Φ(N,γ,α)
34:1353:76917:20:29:72:303:626:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:andX0∈Φ(N,γ,α0),|X|>|X0|andγX>γX0.
34:1354:76951:29:20:72:540:597:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof.The following example is sufficient to establish this result: coalition(3,4,5)is self-enforcing
34:1355:77052:20:20:71:539:577:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:whenα=1/2,but is not self-enforcing when4/7<α<7/12,because(3,4)is now a self-enforcing
34:1356:77138:20:20:71:194:557:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and winning subcoalition.
34:1357:77163:20:20:88:539:537:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Intuitively, higherαturns certain coalitions that were otherwise non-self-enforcing into self-
34:1358:77257:20:19:72:540:517:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing coalitions as expected, but this implies that larger coalitions are now less likely to be
34:1359:77356:19:20:72:539:498:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:self-enforcing and less likely to emerge as the ruling coalition. This, in turn, makes larger coalitions
34:1360:77460:20:20:72:540:478:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:more stable. This proposition therefore establishes that greater power or “agreement” requirements
34:1361:77558:20:20:72:474:458:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:in the form of supermajority rules do not necessarily lead to larger ruling coalitions.
34:1362:77645:20:20:88:539:438:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:The next proposition establishes the complementary result that an increase in the power of an
34:1363:77738:20:20:72:539:418:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:individual can remove him out of the ruling coalition. To state this result, let us use the notation
34:1364:77838:20:29:72:448:398:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:j∈Φ(N,γ,α)to denote a situation in whichX∈Φ(N,γ,α)such thatj∈X.
34:1365:77901:29:20:72:540:369:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 8There exist a societyN,α∈[1/2,1), two mappingsγ,γ0:N→R++satisfying
34:1366:77980:20:19:72:547:349:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f5:C:γi=γ0ifor alli6=j,γj<γ0jsuch thatj∈Φ(N,γ,α),butj/∈Φ(N,γ0,α).Moreover,this
34:1367:78053:19:20:72:538:330:121:g_d0_f5:65:g_d0_f9:C:remains correct if we requirejto be the strongest individual in both cases, i.e.γ0i=γi<γj<γ0j

34:1369:78158:29:20:72:539:281:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof.Takeα=1/2,five playersA,B,C,D,EwithγA=γ0A=2,γB=γ0B=10,γC=γ0C=15,
34:1370:78228:20:20:71:544:261:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f8:C:γD=γ0D=20,γE=21,andγ0E=40.ThenΦ(N,γ,α)={A,D,E},whileΦ(N,γ0,α)=
34:1371:78290:20:20:72:539:241:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f2:B:{B,C,D},soplayerE, who is the most powerful player in both cases, belongs toΦ(N,γ,α)but
34:1372:78377:20:20:72:161:221:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:not toΦ(N,γ0,α).
34:1373:78393:20:19:88:539:201:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 8 shows that being more powerful may be a disadvantage, even for the most powerful
34:1374:78487:19:20:71:539:182:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:player. This raises the question of when the most powerful player will be part of the ruling coalition.
34:1375:78590:20:29:71:313:162:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:This question is addressed in the next proposition.
34:1376:78641:29:20:71:540:133:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 9Suppose thatN={1,...,|N|},α∈[1/2,1),andγ|Nis such thatγ1,...,γ|N|is an
34:1377:78724:20:0:72:378:113:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f7:C:increasing sequence. Consider the gameΓ(N,γ|N,α).Ifγ|N|∈
34:1378:78780:0:8:382:389:125:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:³
34:1379:78781:8:8:395:400:117:65:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f9:F:α
34:1380:78782:8:0:390:405:109:65:g_d0_f17:65:g_d0_f9:F:1−α
34:1381:78785:0:11:409:443:121:121:g_d0_f19:65:g_d0_f17:C:P|N|−1
34:1382:78791:11:0:420:459:110:65:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f6:C:j=2γj,
34:1383:78797:0:8:468:473:117:65:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f9:F:α

34:1390:78912:20:0:71:146:73:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:ruling coalition.
35:1391:78931:0:0:72:215:714:121:g_d0_f1:65:g_d0_f9:C:Proof.Inequalityγ|N|>α1−α

35:1393:78960:11:17:230:539:711:65:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f2:A:j=2γjimplies that any coalition that includes|N|, but excludes

35:1397:79118:16:20:71:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:player|N|does not form a winning coalition by himself. Therefore, eitherNis self-enforcing or
35:1398:79211:20:30:71:406:655:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f2:B:φ(N)does not include the strongest player. This completes the proof.
35:1399:79279:30:26:72:328:625:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f35:C:6.5  Self-Enforcing Coalitions WhenN=3
35:1400:79317:26:20:72:539:599:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:In this subsection, we illustrate the structure of equilibrium ruling coalitions more explicitly for the
35:1401:79421:20:20:72:539:579:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:caseN=3. This representation also shows that even in this most simple environment, an increase
35:1402:79515:20:20:72:462:559:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:inαmight make it less likely that larger coalitions emerge as the ruling coalition.
35:1403:79598:20:20:88:539:539:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:We use the geometric representation already introduced in the Introduction. Generally, the
35:1404:79688:20:20:72:539:519:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:geometric representation of anNplayer game uses the(N−1)-dimensional simplex to depict all
35:1405:79778:20:0:72:490:499:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:potential power allocations, which are represented by points(γ1,...,γN)withγi≥0and
35:1406:79860:0:12:493:505:508:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:P
35:1407:79861:12:16:504:542:496:65:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f8:C:iγi=1
35:1408:79866:16:20:71:539:480:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(where this last equality is without loss of generality).  As discussed in the Introduction, there
35:1409:79964:20:8:71:539:460:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:are two kinds of constraints that define the set of all self-enforcing coalitions: “power constraints”
35:1410:80066:8:15:71:91:452:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:nP
35:1411:80068:15:0:90:142:437:65:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f6:C:j∈Kγj≥α
35:1412:80075:0:12:142:149:452:121:g_d0_f19:121:g_d0_f19:C:o
35:1413:80076:12:20:152:539:440:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:which are always parallel to be respective (K−1)-dimensional facet, and “enforce-
35:1414:80157:20:20:72:329:420:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ment constraints,” which correspond to (quasi-)cones.
35:1415:80210:20:20:88:540:400:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 2 shows the evolution of the set of self-enforcing coalitions asαchanges from1/2(simple
35:1416:80304:20:20:72:539:380:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:majority) to1(unanimous voting rule) for the case withN=3. The set of power configurations
35:1417:80394:20:19:72:539:360:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:such that the grand coalition is the ruling coalition is shaded. Thefirst panel corresponds to the
35:1418:80492:19:20:72:539:341:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:caseα=1/2. For any point(γ1,γ2,γ3)outside the shaded triangle, there is some memberiwho
35:1419:80579:20:20:72:542:321:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:has powerγi>1/2. The second panel corresponds to the case whenαbecomes larger than1/2;it
35:1420:80667:20:20:72:540:301:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:demonstrates that the set of self-enforcing coalitions, while remaining a union of afinite number of
35:1421:80767:20:20:72:540:281:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:convex sets, may have non-convex connected components. Interestingly, the “central coalitions”,
35:1422:80862:20:20:72:539:261:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:i.e. those close to(1/3,1/3,1/3), which were self-enforcing whenα=1/2,cease to be self-enforcing
35:1423:80958:20:19:72:539:241:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:whenαincreases. The reason is that withα>1/2,there is a range of2-person self-enforcing
35:1424:81045:19:20:72:539:222:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions; the fact that they are self-enforcing makes3-person coalitions containing them non-
35:1425:81140:20:20:72:539:202:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:self-enforcing (Figure 2). Whenαis large enough, but still less than2/3,the set of self-enforcing
35:1426:81237:20:20:72:539:182:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalitions coalition set becomes a union of afinite number of convex connected components (namely,
35:1427:81335:20:0:72:403:162:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of three trapezoids). Whenα=2/3,the trapezoids become triangles.
36:1428:81401:0:36:136:472:608:121:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f17:C:α=1212<α<23α>23
36:1429:81416:36:44:282:328:572:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f1:C:Figure 2
36:1430:81424:44:20:88:545:528:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f6:A:The third panel shows that whenα>2/3(and this generalizes straightforwardly toα>
36:1431:81504:20:20:72:540:508:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f2:B:(N−1)/Nfor an arbitraryN),there is a new part to the self-enforcing coalition set around. This
36:1432:81598:20:20:72:539:488:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:demonstrates that the self-enforcing coalition set is non-monotonic inα: the coalitions close to
36:1433:81694:20:19:72:539:468:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f6:C:(1/3,1/3,1/3)are self-enforcing again. This new set of self-enforcing coalitions increases withα
36:1434:81790:19:20:72:539:449:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f6:B:and eventually grows to cover all points whenαapproaches1,but for allαsuch that2/3<α<1,
36:1435:81877:20:20:72:540:429:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:it is a joint of four triangles as shown in the third panel. Obviously, points in the “middle” set
36:1436:81975:20:20:72:539:409:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of self-enforcing coalitions are more stable than other self-enforcing coalitions: even if there is a
36:1437:82076:20:34:72:484:389:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:random shock that eliminates some players, the remainder is a self-enforcing coalition.
36:1438:82163:34:31:72:188:355:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:7Extensions
36:1439:82174:31:20:72:539:324:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:In this section, we discuss two extensions of our basic framework. First, we show how this framework
36:1440:82274:20:20:72:540:304:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:can be applied for thinking about endogenous party formation, and second we show how reallocation
36:1441:82371:20:19:72:539:284:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of power within a group can be beneficial for all group members (which is a form of “giving up the
36:1442:82469:19:30:72:224:265:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:guns” mentioned in footnote 7).
36:1443:82500:30:27:72:200:235:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:7.1  Party Formation
36:1444:82520:27:19:72:539:208:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:If there were no enforcement constraints, theminimal winning coalitionwould always emerge as
36:1445:82612:19:20:72:539:189:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the ruling coalition.15However, we have seen that the ultimate ruling coalition is not necessarily
36:1446:82710:20:20:71:539:169:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the minimal winning coalition. This is because the minimal winning coalition might not be self-
36:1447:82805:20:20:71:539:149:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing (e.g., as is coalition(3,4)in(3,4,5)), and thus cannot form a ruling coalition. What
36:1448:82899:20:20:71:539:129:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:prevents the formation of this coalition is the fact that its members do not to trust each other. If
36:1449:82999:20:16:71:539:109:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:somehow they could enter into binding agreements, the minimum winning coalition could emerge
36:1450:83091:16:14:80:539:93:36:g_d0_f2:82:g_d0_f2:F:15X∈P(N)is a minimal winning coalition withinNifγX>αγNandγX≤γZfor anyZ∈P(N)such that
36:1451:83175:14:0:72:116:79:82:g_d0_f11:82:g_d0_f2:F:γZ>αγN.
37:1452:83184:0:20:72:540:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:as the ultimate willing coalition. In this subsection, we think of party formation as a way of forming
37:1453:83286:20:19:72:540:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:binding agreements among a subset of agents. In particular, we allow some of the players to form
37:1454:83382:19:20:71:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:permanent alliances, effectively merging into a single member with combined power. Another way
37:1455:83476:20:20:71:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:is to allow members of a coalition freely transfer (shares of) their power to each other to make the
37:1456:83576:20:20:71:379:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:coalition self-enforcing, which is explored in the next subsection.
37:1457:83643:20:20:88:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:More specifically, consider the party-formation gameˆΓ0, which is identical to the gameˆΓin
37:1458:83734:20:20:72:539:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:Section 4, except that there is now afirst stage beforeˆΓis played, in which a subset of agents can
37:1459:83833:20:20:72:540:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:form a binding coalition, a “party,” and this party plays the game as a single agent. The result
37:1460:83929:20:19:72:539:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of this party-formation game will be that the minimal winning coalition will form a party and will
37:1461:84027:19:28:72:231:536:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:guarantee power for its members.
37:1462:84059:28:20:72:539:508:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 10Suppose Assumption 1 holds and letXbe the minimal winning coalition, i.e.,
37:1463:84147:20:17:72:540:488:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f5:C:X={Z∈P(X):γZ>αγNand@YwithγY∈(αγN,γZ)}. Then, in the party-formation game
37:1464:84219:17:30:72:212:471:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f5:C:ˆΓ0(N,γ|N,α),theURCisX.
37:1465:84242:30:28:72:442:441:121:g_d0_f1:121:g_d0_f2:B:Proof.The proof follows the steps of the proof of Theorem 2 and is omitted.
37:1466:84317:28:27:72:199:413:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:7.2  Power Exchange
37:1467:84336:27:20:72:540:386:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:We have seen that individuals can be made worse offby having more power. This naturally raises
37:1468:84430:20:20:72:539:366:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the question of whether individuals would like to relinquish their power (for example, give up their
37:1469:84530:20:20:72:539:346:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:guns in the context offighting preceding political decision-making). We now investigate this issue
37:1470:84628:20:20:72:539:326:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:under the assumption thatα=1/2. Our main result is that any minimal winning coalitionXcan
37:1471:84717:20:19:72:539:306:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:redistribute power in such a way that it becomes self-enforcing, and each member ofXis better
37:1472:84810:19:20:72:350:287:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:offthan he would have been without power redistribution.
37:1473:84866:20:20:88:539:267:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f8:A:The next result demonstrates that when the size of the minimal winning coalition exceeds2
37:1474:84955:20:20:72:539:247:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:(i.e., if|X|≥3),Xcan redistribute power to become self-enforcing, with each member becoming
37:1475:85046:20:27:72:402:227:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:strictly better offthan they would have been in the initial allocation.
