39:1630:87892:20:20:71:448:356:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:assumptions 1—3 about the payofffunctions completes the proof of Theorem 5.
39:1631:87967:20:34:88:494:336:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:We also conjecture (but have not yet proved) that Theorem 5 holds for anyα>1/2.
39:1632:88046:34:30:72:189:302:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:8Conclusion
39:1633:88057:30:20:72:539:272:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:The central question of political economy ishow collective choices are made among a group of
39:1634:88149:20:20:72:539:252:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:individuals with conflicting preferences (and potentially different “powers”). We study this question
39:1635:88250:20:20:72:540:232:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:in the context of a game of endogenous coalition formation. We assume that each individual is
39:1636:88343:20:20:72:544:212:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:endowed with a level of political power, which may be derived from his or her specificskillsor
39:1637:88437:20:20:71:540:192:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:access to resources (guns, money etc.). The ruling coalition consists of a subset of the individuals
39:1638:88537:20:19:71:539:172:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:in the society and decides the distribution of resources. The main innovation of our approach is
39:1639:88633:19:20:71:539:153:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:that we also require ruling coalitions to beself-enforcing, in the sense that none of the subcoalitions
39:1640:88736:20:20:71:477:133:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of this ruling coalition should be able to secede and become the new ruling coalition.
39:1641:88822:20:20:88:539:113:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Wefirst model these issues using an axiomatic approach based on four axioms. The two im-
39:1642:88910:20:20:71:539:93:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:portant axioms are that the ruling coalition should be powerful enough (thepower constraint)
39:1643:89002:20:0:71:539:73:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:and that the ruling coalition should be self-enforcing (theenforcement constraint). We prove that
40:1644:89101:0:20:72:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:there exists a unique mapping, which is generically single-valued, that satisfies these axioms. This
40:1645:89201:20:19:71:448:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:provides an axiomatic way of characterizing the ruling coalitions for any game.
40:1646:89280:19:20:88:540:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:We support this notion by showing that the result of our axiomatic analysis also follows from
40:1647:89373:20:20:72:540:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:the “reasonable equilibria” of a dynamic game of coalition formation and also as the unique core
40:1648:89469:20:20:72:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:allocation of a related non-transferable cooperative game.  In particular, we construct a simple
40:1649:89565:20:20:72:540:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:dynamic game that captures the same notions that aruling coalition should have a certain amount
40:1650:89660:20:20:71:539:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:of power and should be self-enforcing (stable). As with other dynamic voting games, this game
40:1651:89753:20:20:71:539:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f5:B:possesses many subgame perfect equilibria. We propose the notion ofsequentially weakly dominant
40:1652:89848:20:19:71:539:555:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f5:C:equilibriumas an equilibrium concept for this and related games (which referred to asagenda-
40:1653:89940:19:20:72:539:536:121:g_d0_f5:121:g_d0_f2:B:setting games). We prove that agenda-setting games always have sequentially weakly dominant
40:1654:90031:20:20:72:539:516:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:equilibria and Markov trembling and perfect equilibria.  Moreover, in our dynamic game, both
40:1655:90123:20:20:71:348:496:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:concepts generically yield a unique equilibrium allocation.
40:1656:90182:20:20:88:539:476:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:After establishing these results on the existenceof equilibria and ruling coalitions in related
40:1657:90277:20:20:71:539:456:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:axiomatic, noncooperative and cooperative games, we present a series of results on the structure of
40:1658:90376:20:31:71:383:436:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:ruling coalitions. In particular,we establish the following results:
40:1659:90444:31:20:88:539:405:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f2:A:•Despite the simplicity of the environment, the ruling coalition can be of any size relative to the
40:1660:90543:20:20:99:539:385:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:society, and may include or exclude more powerful individuals in the society. Consequently,
40:1661:90634:20:29:99:428:365:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:the equilibrium payoffof an individual is not monotone in his power.
40:1662:90702:29:20:88:539:336:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f2:A:•Self-enforcing coalitions are generally “fragile,” especiallyunder majority rule. For example,
40:1663:90797:20:20:99:539:316:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:under majority rule, adding or subtracting one player from a self-enforcing coalition makes
40:1664:90888:20:19:99:539:296:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:it non-self-enforcing. Despite this type of fragility of self-enforcing coalitions, we also show
40:1665:90984:19:20:99:539:277:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:that the ruling coalition is “continuous,” in the sense that two games where the powers of the
40:1666:91078:20:29:99:401:257:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:players are sufficiently close will have the same ruling coalition.
40:1667:91145:29:20:88:539:228:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f2:A:•Somewhat paradoxically, an increase inα–that is an increase in the degree of supermajority
40:1668:91236:20:20:99:539:208:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:necessary to make decisions–does not necessarily lead to larger ruling coalitions. Also, the
40:1669:91328:20:20:99:540:188:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:most powerful individual will be often excluded from the ruling coalition, unless he is powerful
40:1670:91424:20:28:99:539:168:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:enough to win by himself or weak enough so as to be part of smaller self-enforcing coalitions.
40:1671:91518:28:20:88:540:140:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f2:A:•Coalitions of certain sizes are more likely to emerge as the ruling coalition. For example, with
40:1672:91615:20:20:99:539:120:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:majority rule, i.e.,α=1/2, the ruling coalition cannot (generically) consist of two individuals.
40:1673:91711:20:20:99:540:100:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:Moreover, again whenα=1/2,coalitions where members have roughly the same power exist
40:1674:91795:20:0:99:389:80:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:only when the coalition’s size is2k−1wherekis an integer.
41:1675:91854:0:20:88:539:714:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:A:There are a number of natural areas for future study. A similar approach blending axiomatic
41:1676:91945:20:19:71:539:694:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:foundations and dynamic games can be adopted to analyze the structure of ruling coalitions in
41:1677:92038:19:20:71:539:675:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:a more general class of political games, where there are multiple resources to be distributed (or
41:1678:92135:20:20:71:539:655:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:multiple policies over which individuals disagree). Our results on general agenda-setting games
41:1679:92230:20:20:71:539:635:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:suggest that the approach here might be extended to this more general setting. Another interesting
41:1680:92328:20:20:71:539:615:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:area for future research would be to investigate what types of coalitions will form when there is some
41:1681:92430:20:20:71:539:595:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:randomness in the environment, for example, if the powers or preferences of different individuals
41:1682:92527:20:20:71:539:575:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:may change by a small amount after the coalition is formed. Such an approach would allow us to
41:1683:92621:20:19:71:539:555:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:determine the extent to which a coalition is “robust” and also to quantify what “price” the coalition
41:1684:92722:19:20:71:539:536:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:is willing to pay for robustness by including individuals that may not be necessary for obtaining a
41:1685:92821:20:0:71:114:516:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:B:majority.
42:1686:92832:0:23:72:474:714:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:Appendix A: Markov Trembling-Hand Perfect Equilibria
42:1687:92884:23:12:72:539:691:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:We now introduce the notion of Markov Trembling-Hand Perfect Equilibria (MTHPE) and establish both a
42:1688:92984:12:11:71:539:679:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:number of general results about MTHPE and also prove that the results in Section 4 apply with MTHPE
42:1689:93083:11:24:71:466:668:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:in the same way as they do with SWDE. With the terminology in subsection 4.2, we have:
42:1690:93169:24:23:71:333:644:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f2:F:Definition 10A continuation strategyσi,tisMarkovianif

42:1696:93237:0:9:327:333:632:100:g_d0_f19:100:g_d0_f19:F:³

44:1847:100705:12:12:71:271:702:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:thefirst stage, form a pure strategy MTHPE.
44:1848:100748:12:12:88:539:690:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f2:F:(Part 3)Next take any strategy profileσthat forms a MTHPE. This is proved by backward induction
44:1849:100843:12:12:71:539:678:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:on the number of stages in the game. Suppose that the Lemma has been proved for games withq0<qstages.
44:1850:100944:12:12:72:539:666:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Consider an agenda-setting game withqstages and take any MTHPE in it. By induction, this MTHPE,
44:1851:101039:12:12:72:488:654:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:when truncated to any of the game’s proper subgames, forms a SWDE. Consider itsfirst stage.
44:1852:101130:12:11:88:539:642:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Suppose that only one playerimoves at this stage and denote his expected utility (in this MTHPE)
44:1853:101226:11:12:71:539:631:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:from making actionaatfirst stage byuai.Ifactiona∗is an action played with a non-zero probability in
44:1854:101325:12:12:71:539:619:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:equilibrium thenua∗i≥uaiforanyotherfeasibleactiona(otherwise there would exist a payoff-improving
44:1855:101422:12:12:72:540:607:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:deviation).  Hence, all actions played in a MTHPE with a non-zero probability yield the same expected
44:1856:101523:12:12:72:540:595:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:utility for playeri, and this utility is maximum possible over the set of feasible actions. Hence, this MTHPE
44:1857:101632:12:12:72:123:583:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:is a SWDE.
44:1858:101642:12:12:88:539:571:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Now consider the other situation where thefirst stage is a voting stage. Consider a profileσ0consisting of
44:1859:101748:12:12:71:539:559:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:fully mixed strategies and suppose that it isη-close toσfor a smallη. Depending on how other players vote,
44:1860:101854:12:12:71:539:547:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:three mutually exclusive situations are possible: proposal is accepted regardless of how playerivotes, it is
44:1861:101962:12:12:71:540:535:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:rejected regardless of how he votes, and playeriis pivotal; letμ+,μ−,andμpbe the respective probabilities
44:1862:102067:12:12:72:539:523:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:of these events. By definition,μ++μ−+μp=1, and by assumptionμp>0. Voting for the proposal
44:1863:102156:12:12:71:539:511:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:yields(μ++μp)u+0i+μ−u−0iin expectation, voting against it yieldsμ+u+0i+(μ−+μp)u−0iwhereu+0iand
44:1864:102250:12:12:72:533:499:100:g_d0_f6:49:g_d0_f36:F:u−0iarei’s utilities from acceptance and rejection of the proposal if profileσ0is played. Thus, ifu+0i>u−0i
44:1865:102357:12:12:72:540:487:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:then playeri’s sole best response is voting for the proposal, and ifu+0i<u−0iit is voting against it. Ifηis
44:1866:102464:12:12:71:539:475:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:sufficiently small thenu+i>u−iimpliesu+0i>u−0i, and thus by definition of MTHPE playerimust support
44:1867:102563:12:12:71:492:463:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:the proposal in equilibrium with probability one. Similar reasoning applies to the caseu+i<u−i.
44:1868:102658:12:12:88:539:451:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Now take any playeriwho participates in voting. Ifu+i>u−i, then he votes for the proposal in this
44:1869:102755:12:12:72:540:439:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:MTHPE. This is a weakly dominant strategy for him (given continuation strategies of himself and other
44:1870:102856:12:12:72:535:427:100:g_d0_f2:49:g_d0_f36:F:players). Similarly, ifu+i<u−ithen the strategy he plays in this MTHPE is weakly dominant. If,u+i=u−i
44:1871:102957:12:12:72:540:415:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:or the player is never pivotal, any strategy is weakly dominant. Therefore, for any player, the strategy he
44:1872:103064:12:12:72:540:403:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:plays in this MTHPE is weakly dominant, and thus this MTHPE is a SWDE. This completes the induction
44:1873:103163:12:12:72:93:391:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:step.

44:1883:103558:12:12:88:539:264:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:In addition to the existence results, which are of interest in and of themselves, Theorem 6 establishes
44:1884:103661:12:11:72:539:252:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:that while MTHPE and SWDE are not subsets of one another in general, but for agenda-setting games an

44:1887:103964:24:12:72:539:205:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f5:F:Theorem 7Any extensive-form gameˆΓ(N,γ|N,α)has at least one pure strategy MTHPE. Moreover, sup-

45:1896:104644:18:12:72:539:671:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f2:F:Example 4Letα=1/2,|N|=4,N={A,B,C,D},players’powersbegivenbyγA=4,γB=5,γC=6,
45:1897:104718:12:9:71:540:659:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f2:F:γD=8, and players’ utilities from coalitions be given by(2). Take some MTHPEσ∗of the dynamic game
45:1898:104815:9:15:72:539:650:100:g_d0_f8:100:g_d0_f2:F:ˆΓ(N,γ|N,α)and consider the following modificationσX,whereXis one of the six three-player coalitions
45:1899:104915:15:12:72:539:635:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:of players fromN. Before any elimination, ifXis proposed, playerivotes ̃yifi∈Xand votes ̃nifi/∈X;
45:1900:105012:12:12:72:539:623:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:if any proposal other thanXis made, all players vote ̃n.Ifplayeri∈Xis the agenda-setter, he proposes
45:1901:105112:12:12:72:539:611:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:coalitionX, while ifi/∈Xis the agenda-setter, the proposal isN.Afterthefirst elimination has taken
45:1902:105210:12:12:72:269:599:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:place, the corresponding part ofσ∗is played.
45:1903:105254:12:12:88:540:587:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Using the fact thatσ∗is MTHPE, it is easy to see that strategies fromσXare Markovian, it is also
45:1904:105350:12:12:72:540:575:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:straightforward to check thatσXforms a SPNE. Before any elimination occurred, it is not profitable to
45:1905:105451:12:11:71:539:563:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:deviate at the stage of voting. Indeed, if the proposal isX, a deviation by playeri/∈Xdoes not change the
45:1906:105556:11:12:71:543:552:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:outcome of voting, while if playeri∈Xmakes a one-shot deviation, the URC will be eitherXorN;the
45:1907:105651:12:12:71:539:540:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:latter outcome being worse for suchithanX, becausewi(X)>wi(N). If the proposal under consideration
45:1908:105749:12:12:71:539:528:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:is some other proposalY6=X, then none of the players is pivotal, and a deviation will not change the
45:1909:105849:12:12:71:539:516:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:outcome of the voting or the subsequent equilibrium strategies (because strategies are Markovian). It is also
45:1910:105958:12:12:71:539:504:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:straightforward to check that any deviation is not profitable at the stage where proposals are made (mainly
45:1911:106065:12:12:71:539:492:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:because no proposal other thanXmay be accepted in the subsequent voting). After thefirst elimination,
45:1912:106166:12:12:71:540:480:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:strategies fromσ∗are played. Given all this,σXis both a SPNE and a MPE. Evidently, the URC inσXis
45:1913:106263:12:12:71:165:468:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f2:F:Xwith probability1.
45:1914:106282:12:12:88:540:456:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:So, for any of the six three-player coalitions, we have constructed a strategy profile which is a SPNE
45:1915:106384:12:12:71:539:444:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:and, moreover, a MPE. Therefore, none of these refinements help us get a unique prediction of the outcome
45:1916:106489:12:28:71:342:432:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:of the dynamic game (even though Assumption 1) is satisfied.
45:1917:106549:28:18:72:227:404:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f34:C:Dynamic Game Withoutε
45:1918:106570:18:12:72:539:386:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f2:F:Example 5Letα=1/2,|N|=4,N={A,B,C,D},players’powersbegivenbyγA=2,γB=4,γC=7,
45:1919:106644:12:12:71:543:374:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f2:F:γD=10, and players’ utilities from coalitions be given by(2). Theorem 2 establishes that ifε>0,theonly

45:1921:106846:12:12:72:540:350:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:coalition is not self-enforcing). Denote the pure strategy SWDE profile constructed in the proof of Theorem
45:1922:106953:12:12:72:540:338:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2byσ∗; note that it does not depend onε. Because all utilities are continuous inε, we immediately get

45:1926:107274:12:12:71:539:290:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:then playersAandDcast vote ̃y, while playersBandCcast vote ̃n. Let us show that this strategy profile
45:1927:107375:12:12:71:140:278:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:forms a SWDE.
45:1928:107388:12:12:88:539:266:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Suppose thefirst proposal isX0,1={A,D}.  If it is accepted, thenBandCare eliminated, and
45:1929:107476:12:12:71:539:254:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:subsequentlyDeliminatesA. Therefore,u−A=u−B=u−C=0,u−D=1(becauseε=0), while if it is rejected,
45:1930:107569:12:12:71:539:242:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:then, as follows from the construction ofσ∗,{B,C,D}will be the URC, resulting inu−A=0,u−B=4/21,
45:1931:107664:12:12:72:540:230:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f2:F:u−C=1/3,u−D=10/21. It is evident that voting ̃yis weakly dominant forAandD,andvoting ̃nis weakly
45:1932:107760:12:12:71:539:218:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f10:F:dominant forBandC.NowsupposethatAorDis thefirst to make proposal. If he makes proposal{A,D}
45:1933:107851:12:12:71:539:206:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:then, as we have just proved, it will be the URC. If he makes any other proposal, then, as again follows from
45:1934:107960:12:12:71:539:194:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:construction ofσ∗,{B,C,D}will be the URC. Therefore, proposing{A,D}is weakly dominant forAand
45:1935:108053:12:11:71:539:182:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:strictly dominant forD. Finally, in any other node players’ behavior is optimal becauseσ∗coincides with
45:1936:108156:11:12:71:351:171:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f2:F:σ0in the subsequent subgame. Therefore,σ0is indeed a SWDE.
45:1937:108214:12:12:88:539:159:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:In SWDEσ0,theURCis{B,C,D}if thefirst proposer (chosen by Nature) isBorC,and{D}if the
45:1938:108298:12:12:71:540:147:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f2:F:first proposer isAorD(indeed, once proposal{A,D}is accepted, playerAwill be eliminated). Hence,
45:1939:108393:12:12:71:539:135:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:this equilibrium,σ0, features at least two unappealing properties. First, the outcome may depend on the
45:1940:108496:12:12:71:539:123:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:order of proposals. Second, players that will be eliminated anyway (Ain this example) may have have a
45:1941:108597:12:12:71:539:111:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:non-trivial effect on the outcome, depending on how they vote when they are indifferent. Introducing small
45:1942:108703:12:12:71:539:99:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:organizational costsε>0allows us to get rid of these effects and get equilibria where the ultimate ruling
45:1943:108808:12:0:71:337:87:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:coalition that emerges in equilibrium is uniquelydetermined.

54:2529:134837:12:12:88:539:128:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:This completes the proof of the induction step, which proves the one-to-one correspondence between
